## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate-law ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard formulation of reaction kinetics as an ODE rate law. With only (t, A) available, the most plausible structures are order-based rate laws, equilibrium/relaxation forms, and time-varying (externally driven) rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of concentration; e.g., catalyst saturated, constant source removal)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction when the other reactant is proportional to A)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical global kinetics / lumped mechanisms)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady-state concentration c1)
- Constant feed + linear removal (CSTR-like): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (source term plus first-order loss)
- Autocatalytic/self-limiting form: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (growth-like intermediate/autocatalysis with finite capacity)
- Bistable / multiple fixed points: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) * (A - c2) (two equilibria; switch-like kinetics)
- Saturating (capacity-limited) consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (transitions from first-order at low A to zero-order at high A)
- Substrate-inhibition-like suppression at high A: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1 + c2 * A**2) (rate decreases again at high A due to inhibition/aggregation)
- Time-varying rate constant (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (changing conditions/catalyst activity over time)
- Time-varying rate constant (deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t) (effective rate slows due to catalyst deactivation or reagent depletion elsewhere)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (light-driven/periodic feed or temperature cycling reflected as k(t))
- Mass-transfer/aging-limited form: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (t + c1)**c2 (effective rate diminishes with time due to boundary-layer growth or fouling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is strictly negative and proportional to A, expect exponential decay with a constant half-life (signature of first-order kinetics).
- If dA_dt scales like -A**2 (or higher power), decay is much faster at early times and slows strongly later (bimolecular/global higher-order behavior).
- If the fitted exponent in -A**c is fractional (0<c<1), it often indicates heterogeneous/diffusion-limited or distributed-rate processes rather than a single elementary step.
- A factor (A - c1) implies a steady-state/equilibrium concentration at A = c1; the sign of dA_dt flips around that point (relaxation dynamics).
- A constant term plus -k*A (c0 - c1*A) suggests an open system with production/inflow balanced by removal (well-mixed reactor/turnover).
- An A*(c1 - A) factor indicates self-limitation with a peak rate near A = c1/2 and zero rate at A=0 and A=c1 (autocatalysis with depletion/capacity).
- Rational forms like A/(A+c) indicate a transition between kinetic regimes (low-A linear dependence vs high-A saturation), consistent with limited active sites or enzyme/catalyst saturation.
- Extra suppression at high A via (A + c1 + c2*A**2) in the denominator points to inhibition/aggregation/viscosity effects that reduce effective reaction rate at high concentration.
- Explicit time dependence in the coefficient of A (e.g., (c0+c1*t) or exp(-c*t)) suggests non-stationary conditions such as catalyst deactivation, heating/cooling ramps, or unmodeled reactant depletion.
- Sinusoidal dependence on t in the rate constant suggests periodic external driving (illumination cycles, pulsed feeding, periodic temperature control) rather than intrinsic kinetics.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK5)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) + c1*_f*A**c2
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is a fixed function of **A only** (no t-dependence):
\[
f(A)=0.5229500625821207\,A^{1/3}-0.3254156367450257\,A^{1/2}.
\]
So any matching candidate must (i) be independent of **t** after parameter choices, and (ii) be exactly a linear combination of \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^{1/2}\) with those exact coefficients, with **no extra terms** (no constants, no \(A\), no logs, no rationals, etc.).

---

### 1.
Has terms \(A c0\), rational-in-\(A\) pieces, \(A^{c6}c7\), and \(c8/(A+c5)\). You can zero out many terms, but you cannot produce **two different fractional powers** \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^{1/2}\) simultaneously: there is only one power term \(A^{c6}c7\). Rationals cannot equal fractional powers for all \(A\). **No match.**

### 2.
Contains \(A\), \(A^{c1}\), logs, constant, and \(A^{-1/4}\). Logs can be removed by setting coefficients to 0, but you still cannot get both \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^{1/2}\): only one free power \(A^{c1}\) plus fixed \(A\) unless its coefficient is forced (but \(A\) term here is literal “+ A”, cannot be removed). **No match.**

### 3.
Same issue as (1): only one power term \(A^{c6}c7\) plus rational terms. Cannot create both \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^{1/2}\). **No match.**

### 4.
Has literal “+ A” again (cannot be removed), plus one power \(A^{c1}\), logs absent here but still only one adjustable power and unavoidable \(A\). **No match.**

### 5.
Has explicit \(t\)-dependence via \(\exp(c2/(c3+t))\) and \(t/(A c5+c6)\), plus \(1/A\). You could try to kill t-dependence by setting coefficients to 0, but then remaining terms are linear in \(A\) and/or \(1/A\), not fractional powers. **No match.**

### 6.
Contains literal “+ A” (unremovable), plus linear \(A\) terms, log, constant, and \(A^{-1/4}\). Cannot equal GT. **No match.**

### 7.
Has multiple unavoidable \(t\)-dependent structures unless coefficients are zeroed; remaining includes literal “+ A” and \(A^{-1/4}\). Cannot match. **No match.**

### 8.
Form: \(A c0 + c2 A^{c1} + c4 A^{c3} + c5\).
This can represent a sum of **two power laws** plus optional linear and constant. Set \(c0=0\), \(c5=0\). Choose exponents \(c1=1/3\), \(c3=1/2\). Then set coefficients \(c2=0.5229500625821207\) and \(c4=-0.3254156367450257\). This exactly equals GT for all \(A\). **Match.**

### 9.
Has \(t\)-dependent exp and \(t/(A c6+c7)\). Killing those leaves only linear \(A\) terms, not fractional powers. **No match.**

### 10.
Has \(t\)-dependent rational terms and only one power \(A^{c1}\) plus \(A^{-1/4}\). Cannot form both \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^{1/2}\). **No match.**

### 11.
Rational functions in \(A\) plus constant. No fractional-power terms. **No match.**

### 12.
Linear \(A\) plus rational-in-\(A\) plus constant. No fractional powers. **No match.**

### 13.
Has \(t\)-dependent term \(c3/(c4+t)\) and only one power \(A^{c1}\) plus \(A^{-1/4}\). Even removing t-term, cannot get both \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^{1/2}\). **No match.**

### 14.

### 15.

### 16.

### 17.

### 18.

**GT: 0.5229500625821207·A^(1/3) - 0.3254156367450257·√A**

**Candidate 1:** `A*c0 + A*c1/(A + c2) + A*c3/(A*c4 + c5) + A^c6*c7 + c8/(A + c5)`

Can set c0=0 to kill linear A term. The terms A*c1/(A+c2) and A*c3/(A*c4+c5) are rational functions of A. A^c6*c7 can give A^(1/3) with c6=1/3. But we also need A^(1/2). The rational functions A/(A+c) = 1 - c/(A+c), which cannot produce A^(1/2). We'd need another power-law term. Can we zero out the rational terms? Set c1=0, c3=0, c8=0. Then we have A^c6*c7, which gives only one power of A. We need two distinct powers. **Cannot match.**

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]
